<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">North America</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"North American" redirects here. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Northern_America" title="Northern America">Northern America</a> or <a href="/wiki/Northern_United_States" title="Northern United States">Northern United States</a>.</div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_populous_North_America_(physical,_political,_population).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3287" data-file-width="4061" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Map_of_populous_North_America_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29.jpg/220px-Map_of_populous_North_America_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Map_of_populous_North_America_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29.jpg/330px-Map_of_populous_North_America_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Map_of_populous_North_America_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29.jpg/440px-Map_of_populous_North_America_%28physical%2C_political%2C_population%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_populous_North_America_(physical,_political,_population).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of populous North America showing physical, political and population characteristics as per 2018</div></div></div>
<p><b>North America</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a> and almost entirely within the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[b]</a></sup> It is bordered to the north by the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>, to the east by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, to the southeast by <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, and to the west and south by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. Because it is on the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Tectonic Plate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> is included as a part of North America geographically.
</p><p>North America covers an area of about 24,709,000 square kilometres (9,540,000 square miles), about 16.5% of <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>'s land area and about 4.8% of its total surface. North America is the third-largest continent by area, following <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_continents_and_continental_subregions_by_population" title="List of continents and continental subregions by population">fourth</a> by population after Asia, Africa, and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. In 2013, its population was estimated at nearly 579 million people in <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_North_America" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in North America">23 independent states</a>, or about 7.5% of the world's population. In <a href="/wiki/Americas_(terminology)#Human_geography" title="Americas (terminology)">human geography</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">English-speaking world</a> outside the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, particularly in Canada, "North America" and "North American" can refer to just Canada and the United States together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoC_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-MoC-9">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>North America was reached by its <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_the_Americas" title="Settlement of the Americas">first human populations</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Last_Glacial_Period" title="Last Glacial Period">Last Glacial Period</a>, via crossing the <a href="/wiki/Beringia" title="Beringia">Bering land bridge</a> approximately 20,000 to 17,000 years ago. The so-called <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">Paleo-Indian</a> period is taken to have lasted until about 10,000 years ago (the beginning of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaic_period_in_North_America" title="Archaic period in North America">Archaic or Meso-Indian</a> period). The <a href="/wiki/Classic_stage" title="Classic stage">classic stage</a> spans roughly the 6th to 13th centuries. The first recorded Europeans to visit North America (other than Greenland) were <a href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_North_America" title="Norse colonization of North America">the Norse</a> around 1000 AD. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>'s arrival in 1492 sparked <a href="/wiki/Columbian_exchange" title="Columbian exchange">a transatlantic exchange</a> which included <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_migrations" title="Transatlantic migrations">migrations</a> of <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European settlers</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a>. Present-day cultural and ethnic patterns reflect interactions between European colonists, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a>, immigrants from Europe, Asia, and the descendants of these groups.
</p><p>Owing to Europe's colonization of the Americas, most North Americans speak European languages such as English, Spanish or French, and their cultures commonly reflect <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western traditions</a>. However, in parts of Canada, the United States, Mexico, and <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, there are indigenous populations continuing their cultural traditions and speaking native languages.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Etymology"></span>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Naming_of_the_Americas" title="Naming of the Americas">Naming of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turtle_Island_(Native_American_folklore)" title="Turtle Island (Native American folklore)">Turtle Island (Native American folklore)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vinland" title="Vinland">Vinland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historisch_Nordamerika_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1682" data-file-width="2249" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Historisch_Nordamerika_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Historisch_Nordamerika_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Historisch_Nordamerika_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Historisch_Nordamerika_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Historisch_Nordamerika_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Historisch_Nordamerika_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historisch_Nordamerika_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of North America, from 1621</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> are usually accepted as having been named after the Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a> by the German cartographers <a href="/wiki/Martin_Waldseem%C3%BCller" title="Martin Waldseemüller">Martin Waldseemüller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Ringmann" title="Matthias Ringmann">Matthias Ringmann</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> Vespucci, who explored South America between 1497 and 1502, was the first <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> to suggest that the Americas were not the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>, but a different landmass previously unknown by Europeans. In 1507, Waldseemüller produced a world map, in which he placed the word "America" on the continent of South America, in the middle of what is today Brazil. He explained the rationale for the name in the accompanying book <i>Cosmographiae Introductio</i>: <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">"ab Americo inventore ... quasi Americi terram sive Americam</i></span> (from Americus the discoverer ... as if it were the land of Americus, thus America)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> What was known about North American continent was referred to as <i><b>Parias</b></i> above what is today Mexico<i>.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> A 1553 world map published by <a href="/wiki/Petrus_Apianus" title="Petrus Apianus">Petrus Apianus</a> in his <i>Charta Cosmographica, Cum Ventorum Propria Natura et Operatione</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> North America was called <i><b>Baccalearum</b></i>, meaning "realm of the Cod fish", in reference to the abundance of Cod fish on the east coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>For Waldseemüller, no one should object to the naming of the land after its discoverer. He used the Latinized version of Vespucci's name (Americus Vespucius), but in its feminine form "America", following the examples of "Europa", "Asia" and "Africa". Later, other mapmakers extended the name <i>America</i> to the northern continent, dropping the usage of "Parias". In 1538, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerard_Mercator" title="Gerard Mercator">Gerard Mercator</a> used <i>America</i> on his map of the world for all the Western Hemisphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohen_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-18">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some argue that because the convention is to use the surname for naming discoveries (except in the case of royalty), the derivation from "Amerigo Vespucci" could be put in question.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> In 1874, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Belt" title="Thomas Belt">Thomas Belt</a> published the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">indigenous</a> name of the <a href="/wiki/Amerrisque_Mountains" title="Amerrisque Mountains">Amerrisque Mountains</a> of Central America;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> the next year, <a href="/wiki/Jules_Marcou" title="Jules Marcou">Jules Marcou</a> suggested that the name of the continent stemmed from that of the mountain range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup> Marcou corresponded with <a href="/wiki/Augustus_Le_Plongeon" title="Augustus Le Plongeon">Augustus Le Plongeon</a>, who wrote: "The name AMERICA or AMERRIQUE in the <a href="/wiki/Mayan_languages" title="Mayan languages">Mayan language</a> means, a country of perpetually strong wind, or the Land of the Wind, and ... the [suffixes] can mean ... a spirit that breathes, life itself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohen_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-18">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gerardus_Mercator" title="Gerardus Mercator">Mercator</a> on <a href="/wiki/Mercator_1569_world_map" title="Mercator 1569 world map">his map</a> called North America "America or New India" (<i>America sive India Nova</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> called its territories in North and South America "Las Indias"; the state body overseeing them was the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Indies" title="Council of the Indies">Council of the Indies</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent"><span id="Usage_of_the_term">Extent</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AS16-118-18880_(21709833861).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4200" data-file-width="4275" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/AS16-118-18880_%2821709833861%29.jpg/220px-AS16-118-18880_%2821709833861%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/AS16-118-18880_%2821709833861%29.jpg/330px-AS16-118-18880_%2821709833861%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/AS16-118-18880_%2821709833861%29.jpg/440px-AS16-118-18880_%2821709833861%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AS16-118-18880_(21709833861).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The totality of North America seen by the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_16" title="Apollo 16">Apollo 16</a> crew, with <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> being covered by clouds</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> formally recognizes "North America" as comprising three areas: <a href="/wiki/Northern_America" title="Northern America">Northern America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. This has been formally defined by the UN Statistics Division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>"Northern America", as a term distinct from "North America", excludes Central America, which itself may or may not include <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Central_America#Different_definitions" title="Central America">Central America § Different definitions</a>). In the limited context of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a>, the term covers Canada, the United States, and Mexico, which are the three signatories of that treaty.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, and the countries of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> use a <a href="/wiki/Continent#Number" title="Continent">six-continent model</a>, with the Americas viewed as a single continent and <i>North America</i> designating a subcontinent comprising Canada, the United States, Mexico, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Pierre_et_Miquelon" title="Saint Pierre et Miquelon">Saint Pierre et Miquelon</a> (politically part of France), and often <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>North America has been historically referred to by other names. Spanish North America (<a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>) was often referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Northern_America" title="Northern America">Northern America</a></i>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and this was the <a href="/wiki/Solemn_Act_of_the_Declaration_of_Independence_of_Northern_America" title="Solemn Act of the Declaration of Independence of Northern America">first official name</a> given to Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AGN_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-AGN-31">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Canada" title="List of regions of Canada">List of regions of Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_the_United_States" title="List of regions of the United States">List of regions of the United States</a></div>
<p>Geographically, the North American continent has many regions and subregions. These include cultural, economic, and geographic regions. Economic regions included those formed by trade blocs, such as the North American Trade Agreement bloc and Central American Trade Agreement. Linguistically and culturally, the continent could be divided into <a href="/wiki/Anglo-America" title="Anglo-America">Anglo-America</a> and Latin America. Anglo-America includes most of Northern America, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, and Caribbean islands with English-speaking populations (though sub-national entities, such as <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, have large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">Francophone</a> populations; in Quebec, French is the sole official language<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-language_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-language-32">[30]</a></sup>).
</p><p>The southern part of the North American continent is composed of two regions. These are Central America and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaCA_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaCA-33">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> The north of the continent maintains recognized regions as well. In contrast to the common definition of "North America", which encompasses the whole continent, the term "North America" is sometimes used to refer only to Mexico, Canada, the United States, and Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAGreenland_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIAGreenland-35">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CountryReports_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-CountryReports-36">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eNotes_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-eNotes-37">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trilateral_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trilateral-38">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term Northern America refers to the northernmost countries and territories of North America: the United States, Bermuda, St. Pierre and Miquelon, Canada, and Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> Although the term does not refer to a unified region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Middle_America_(Americas)" title="Middle America (Americas)">Middle America</a>—not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern United States</a>—groups the regions of Mexico, Central America, and the Caribbean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>North America's largest countries by land area, Canada and the United States, also have well-defined and recognized regions. In the case of Canada, these are (from east to west) <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Canada" title="Central Canada">Central Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Prairies" title="Canadian Prairies">Canadian Prairies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia_Coast" title="British Columbia Coast">British Columbia Coast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">Northern Canada</a>. These regions also contain many subregions. In the case of the United States—and in accordance with the US Census Bureau definitions—these regions are: <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_(United_States)" title="Mid-Atlantic (United States)">Mid-Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_states" title="South Atlantic states">South Atlantic states</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_North_Central_states" title="East North Central states">East North Central states</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_North_Central_states" title="West North Central states">West North Central states</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_South_Central_states" title="East South Central states">East South Central states</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_South_Central_states" title="West South Central states">West South Central states</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_states" title="Mountain states">Mountain states</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">Pacific states</a>. Regions shared between both nations include the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_region" title="Great Lakes region">Great Lakes region</a>. <a href="/wiki/Megalopolis" title="Megalopolis">Megalopolises</a> have formed between both nations in the case of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_megalopolis" title="Great Lakes megalopolis">Great Lakes Megaregion</a>.
</p><p><span data-sort-value="1000000000000000000♠"></span>
</p>
<h3><span id="Countries.2C_dependencies.2C_and_other_territories"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries,_dependencies,_and_other_territories">Countries, dependencies, and other territories</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_North_America" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in North America">List of sovereign states and dependent territories in North America</a></div>

<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shield_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg"><img alt="Shield of the Turks and Caicos Islands.svg" data-file-height="387" data-file-width="287" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Shield_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg/30px-Shield_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Shield_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg/45px-Shield_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Shield_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg/60px-Shield_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg.png 2x" width="30"/></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_characteristics">Natural characteristics</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography"><span id="Geography_and_extent">Geography</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_North_America" title="Geography of North America">Geography of North America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Physical_Features_of_North_America_map_by_Tom_Patterson_v._1.01,_meters.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="16495" data-file-width="15930" decoding="async" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Physical_Features_of_North_America_map_by_Tom_Patterson_v._1.01%2C_meters.jpg/260px-Physical_Features_of_North_America_map_by_Tom_Patterson_v._1.01%2C_meters.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Physical_Features_of_North_America_map_by_Tom_Patterson_v._1.01%2C_meters.jpg/390px-Physical_Features_of_North_America_map_by_Tom_Patterson_v._1.01%2C_meters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Physical_Features_of_North_America_map_by_Tom_Patterson_v._1.01%2C_meters.jpg/520px-Physical_Features_of_North_America_map_by_Tom_Patterson_v._1.01%2C_meters.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Physical_Features_of_North_America_map_by_Tom_Patterson_v._1.01,_meters.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Landform" title="Landform">Landforms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Land_cover" title="Land cover">land cover</a> of North America</div></div></div>
<p>North America occupies the northern portion of the landmass generally referred to as the New World, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, or simply America (which, in many countries is considered as a single <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOC_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-IOC-59">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oceano_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oceano-60">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cincocontinentes_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-cincocontinentes-61">[53]</a></sup> with North America a <a href="/wiki/Continent#Subcontinents" title="Continent">subcontinent</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica-northamerica_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-northamerica-63">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[56]</a></sup> North America is the third-largest continent by area, following <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[58]</a></sup> North America's only land connection to <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> is at the Isthmus of Darian/Isthmus of Panama. The continent is delimited on the southeast by most geographers at the <a href="/wiki/Dari%C3%A9n_Gap" title="Darién Gap">Darién watershed</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>-Panama border, placing almost all of Panama within North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-North_America_Atlas_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-North_America_Atlas-69">[61]</a></sup> Alternatively, some geologists physiographically locate its southern limit at the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Tehuantepec" title="Isthmus of Tehuantepec">Isthmus of Tehuantepec</a>, Mexico, with Central America extending southeastward to South America from this point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[62]</a></sup> The Caribbean islands, or West Indies, are considered part of North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica-northamerica_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-northamerica-63">[55]</a></sup> The continental coastline is long and irregular. The <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> is the largest body of water indenting the continent, followed by <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">Hudson Bay</a>. Others include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">Gulf of Saint Lawrence</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">Gulf of California</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saguaro_National_Park_-_Flickr_-_Joe_Parks.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2618" data-file-width="3927" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Saguaro_National_Park_-_Flickr_-_Joe_Parks.jpg/220px-Saguaro_National_Park_-_Flickr_-_Joe_Parks.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Saguaro_National_Park_-_Flickr_-_Joe_Parks.jpg/330px-Saguaro_National_Park_-_Flickr_-_Joe_Parks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Saguaro_National_Park_-_Flickr_-_Joe_Parks.jpg/440px-Saguaro_National_Park_-_Flickr_-_Joe_Parks.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saguaro_National_Park_-_Flickr_-_Joe_Parks.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sonoran_Desert" title="Sonoran Desert">Sonoran Desert</a> in Arizona</div></div></div>
<p>Before the Central American isthmus formed, the region had been underwater. The islands of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> delineate a submerged former <a href="/wiki/Land_bridge" title="Land bridge">land bridge</a>, which had connected North and South America via what are now <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.
</p><p>There are numerous islands off the continent's coasts; principally, the Arctic Archipelago, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_%26_Caicos" title="Turks &amp; Caicos">Turks &amp; Caicos</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> (some of which are in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere" title="Eastern Hemisphere">Eastern Hemisphere</a> proper), the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Archipelago" title="Alexander Archipelago">Alexander Archipelago</a>, the many thousand islands of the British Columbia Coast, and Newfoundland. Greenland, a self-governing Danish island, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">world's largest</a>, is on the same <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tectonic_plate" title="Tectonic plate">tectonic plate</a> (the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Plate</a>) and is part of North America geographically. In a geologic sense, Bermuda is not part of the Americas, but an oceanic island that was formed on the fissure of the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Ridge" title="Mid-Atlantic Ridge">Mid-Atlantic Ridge</a> over 100 million years ago. The nearest landmass to it is <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras" title="Cape Hatteras">Cape Hatteras</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>. However, Bermuda is often thought of as part of North America, especially given its historical, political and cultural ties to <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> and other parts of the continent.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moraine_Lake_17092005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Moraine_Lake_17092005.jpg/220px-Moraine_Lake_17092005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Moraine_Lake_17092005.jpg/330px-Moraine_Lake_17092005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Moraine_Lake_17092005.jpg/440px-Moraine_Lake_17092005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moraine_Lake_17092005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Moraine_Lake" title="Moraine Lake">Moraine Lake</a> in <a href="/wiki/Banff_National_Park" title="Banff National Park">Banff National Park</a></div></div></div>
<p>The vast majority of North America is on the North American Plate. Parts of western Mexico, including Baja California, and of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, including the cities of <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_California" title="Santa Cruz, California">Santa Cruz</a>, lie on the eastern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Plate" title="Pacific Plate">Pacific Plate</a>, with the two plates meeting along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Andreas_fault" title="San Andreas fault">San Andreas fault</a>. The southernmost portion of the continent and much of the West Indies lie on the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a>, whereas the <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Fuca_Plate" title="Juan de Fuca Plate">Juan de Fuca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cocos_Plate" title="Cocos Plate">Cocos plates</a> border the North American Plate on its western frontier.
</p><p>The continent can be divided into four great regions (each of which contains many subregions): the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a> stretching from the Gulf of Mexico to the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">Canadian Arctic</a>; the geologically young, mountainous west, including the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Basin" title="Great Basin">Great Basin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_California" title="Geography of California">California</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>; the raised but relatively flat plateau of the Canadian Shield in the northeast; and the varied eastern region, which includes the Appalachian Mountains, the coastal plain along the Atlantic seaboard, and the Florida peninsula. Mexico, with its long <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateaus</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_cordillera" title="American cordillera">cordilleras</a>, falls largely in the western region, although the eastern coastal plain does extend south along the Gulf.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nuuk_city_below_Sermitsiaq.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1119" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Nuuk_city_below_Sermitsiaq.JPG/220px-Nuuk_city_below_Sermitsiaq.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Nuuk_city_below_Sermitsiaq.JPG/330px-Nuuk_city_below_Sermitsiaq.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Nuuk_city_below_Sermitsiaq.JPG/440px-Nuuk_city_below_Sermitsiaq.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nuuk_city_below_Sermitsiaq.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Nuuk</a>, the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a></div></div></div>
<p>The western mountains are split in the middle into the main range of the Rockies and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Ranges" title="Pacific Coast Ranges">coast ranges</a> in California, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, with the Great Basin—a lower area containing smaller ranges and low-lying deserts—in between. The highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Denali" title="Denali">Denali</a> in Alaska.
</p><p>The <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120722022527/http://egsc.usgs.gov/isb/pubs/booklets/elvadist/elvadist.html" rel="nofollow">United States Geographical Survey (USGS)</a> states that the geographic center of North America is "6 miles [10 km] west of <a href="/wiki/Balta,_North_Dakota" title="Balta, North Dakota">Balta, Pierce County, North Dakota</a>" at about <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1073938472">.mw-parser-output .geo-default,.mw-parser-output .geo-dms,.mw-parser-output .geo-dec{display:inline}.mw-parser-output .geo-nondefault,.mw-parser-output .geo-multi-punct{display:none}.mw-parser-output .longitude,.mw-parser-output .latitude{white-space:nowrap}</style><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=North_America&amp;params=48_10_N_100_10_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">48°10′N</span> <span class="longitude">100°10′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">48.167°N 100.167°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">48.167; -100.167</span></span></span></a></span>, about 24 kilometres (15 mi) from <a href="/wiki/Rugby,_North_Dakota" title="Rugby, North Dakota">Rugby, North Dakota</a>. The USGS further states that "No marked or monumented point has been established by any government agency as the geographic center of either the 50 States, the conterminous United States, or the North American continent." Nonetheless, there is a 4.6-metre (15 ft) field stone <a href="/wiki/Obelisk" title="Obelisk">obelisk</a> in Rugby claiming to mark the center. The North American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_pole_of_inaccessibility" title="Continental pole of inaccessibility">continental pole of inaccessibility</a> is located 1,650 km (1,030 mi) from the nearest coastline, between <a href="/wiki/Allen,_South_Dakota" title="Allen, South Dakota">Allen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyle,_South_Dakota" title="Kyle, South Dakota">Kyle, South Dakota</a> at <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1073938472" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=North_America&amp;params=43.36_N_101.97_W_&amp;title=Pole+of+Inaccessibility+North+America"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">43°22′N</span> <span class="longitude">101°58′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="vcard"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">43.36°N 101.97°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">43.36; -101.97</span></span><span style="display:none">﻿ (<span class="fn org">Pole of Inaccessibility North America</span>)</span></span></span></a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PIA_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-PIA-71">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_North_America" title="Geology of North America">Geology of North America</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Geologic_history">Geologic history</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png/260px-NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png/390px-NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png/520px-NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Principal hydrological divides of Canada, the United States and Mexico</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Laurentia" title="Laurentia">Laurentia</a> is an ancient <a href="/wiki/Craton" title="Craton">craton</a> which forms the geologic core of North America; it formed between 1.5 and 1.0 billion years ago during the <a href="/wiki/Proterozoic" title="Proterozoic">Proterozoic</a> eon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[64]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">Canadian Shield</a> is the largest exposure of this craton. From the Late <a href="/wiki/Paleozoic" title="Paleozoic">Paleozoic</a> to Early <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic" title="Mesozoic">Mesozoic</a> eras, North America was joined with the other modern-day continents as part of the supercontinent <a href="/wiki/Pangaea" title="Pangaea">Pangaea</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> to its east. One of the results of the formation of Pangaea was the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Taconic_orogeny" title="Taconic orogeny">formed</a> some 480 million years ago, making it among the oldest mountain ranges in the world. When Pangaea began to rift around 200 million years ago, North America became part of <a href="/wiki/Laurasia" title="Laurasia">Laurasia</a>, before it separated from Eurasia as its own continent during the mid-<a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-73">[65]</a></sup> The Rockies and other western mountain ranges began forming around this time from a period of mountain building called the <a href="/wiki/Laramide_orogeny" title="Laramide orogeny">Laramide orogeny</a>, between 80 and 55 million years ago. The formation of the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a> that connected the continent to South America arguably occurred approximately 12 to 15 million years ago,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Origins_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Origins-74">[66]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> (as well as many other northern freshwater lakes and rivers) were carved by receding glaciers about 10,000 years ago.
</p><p>North America is the source of much of what humanity knows about <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geologic_time" title="Geologic time">geologic time</a> periods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinopedia-american_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-dinopedia-american-75">[67]</a></sup> The geographic area that would later become the United States has been the source of more varieties of <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaurs</a> than any other modern country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinopedia-american_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-dinopedia-american-75">[67]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">paleontologist</a> Peter Dodson, this is primarily due to stratigraphy, climate and geography, human resources, and history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinopedia-american_75-2"><a href="#cite_note-dinopedia-american-75">[67]</a></sup> Much of the Mesozoic Era is represented by exposed outcrops in the many arid regions of the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinopedia-american_75-3"><a href="#cite_note-dinopedia-american-75">[67]</a></sup> The most significant <a href="/wiki/Late_Jurassic" title="Late Jurassic">Late Jurassic</a> dinosaur-bearing fossil deposit in North America is the <a href="/wiki/Morrison_Formation" title="Morrison Formation">Morrison Formation</a> of the western United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jurassicdistribution_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-jurassicdistribution-76">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canadian_geology">Canadian geology</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USGS_Geologic_Map_of_North_America.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6798" data-file-width="7000" decoding="async" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/USGS_Geologic_Map_of_North_America.jpg/260px-USGS_Geologic_Map_of_North_America.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/USGS_Geologic_Map_of_North_America.jpg/390px-USGS_Geologic_Map_of_North_America.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/USGS_Geologic_Map_of_North_America.jpg/520px-USGS_Geologic_Map_of_North_America.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USGS_Geologic_Map_of_North_America.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geologic map of North America published by USGS</div></div></div>
<p>Geologically, Canada is one of the oldest regions in the world, with more than half of the region consisting of <a href="/wiki/Precambrian" title="Precambrian">precambrian</a> rocks that have been above sea level since the beginning of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palaeozoic" title="Palaeozoic">Palaeozoic</a> era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marianopolis_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marianopolis-77">[69]</a></sup> Canada's mineral resources are diverse and extensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marianopolis_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marianopolis-77">[69]</a></sup> Across the Canadian Shield and in the north there are large iron, nickel, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, copper, gold, lead, <a href="/wiki/Molybdenum" title="Molybdenum">molybdenum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> reserves. Large diamond concentrations have been recently developed in the Arctic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[70]</a></sup> making Canada one of the world's largest producers. Throughout the Shield, there are many mining towns extracting these minerals. The largest, and best known, is <a href="/wiki/Greater_Sudbury" title="Greater Sudbury">Sudbury</a>, Ontario. Sudbury is an exception to the normal process of forming minerals in the Shield since there is significant evidence that the <a href="/wiki/Sudbury_Basin" title="Sudbury Basin">Sudbury Basin</a> is an ancient <a href="/wiki/Meteorite" title="Meteorite">meteorite</a> <a href="/wiki/Impact_crater" title="Impact crater">impact crater</a>. The nearby, but less known <a href="/wiki/Temagami_Magnetic_Anomaly" title="Temagami Magnetic Anomaly">Temagami Magnetic Anomaly</a> has striking similarities to the Sudbury Basin. Its magnetic anomalies are very similar to the Sudbury Basin, and so it could be a second metal-rich impact crater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GH_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-GH-79">[71]</a></sup> The Shield is also covered by vast boreal forests that support an important logging industry.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_geology">United States geology</span></h4>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" title="Continental United States">lower 48 US states</a> can be divided into roughly five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physiography" title="Physiography">physiographic</a> provinces:
</p>
<ol><li>The American cordillera</li>
<li>The Canadian Shield<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marianopolis_77-2"><a href="#cite_note-Marianopolis-77">[69]</a></sup> Northern portion of the upper midwestern United States.</li>
<li>The stable platform</li>
<li>The coastal plain</li>
<li>The Appalachian <a href="/wiki/Orogeny" title="Orogeny">orogenic</a> belt</li></ol>
<p>The geology of <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> is typical of that of the cordillera, while the major islands of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> consist of <a href="/wiki/Neogene" title="Neogene">Neogene</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanics</a> erupted over a <a href="/wiki/Hotspot_(geology)" title="Hotspot (geology)">hot spot</a>.
</p>

href="/wiki/Craton" title="Craton">cratons</a> and basement rocks</div></div></div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_American_geology">Central American geology</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/220px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/330px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/440px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FAD4AF; color:black;"> </span> Central America rests in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a>.</div></div></div></div>
<p>Central America is geologically active with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanic_eruption" title="Volcanic eruption">volcanic eruptions</a> and earthquakes occurring from time to time. In 1976 Guatemala was hit by a <a href="/wiki/1976_Guatemala_earthquake" title="1976 Guatemala earthquake">major earthquake</a>, killing 23,000 people; Managua, the capital of Nicaragua, was devastated by earthquakes in 1931 and 1972, the last one killing about 5,000 people; three earthquakes devastated El Salvador, one in 1986 and two in 2001; one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_Costa_Rica_earthquake" title="2009 Costa Rica earthquake">earthquake</a> devastated northern and central Costa Rica in 2009, killing at least 34 people; in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_Honduras_earthquake" title="2009 Honduras earthquake">Honduras</a> a powerful earthquake killed seven people in 2009.
</p><p>Volcanic eruptions are common in the region. In 1968 the <a href="/wiki/Arenal_Volcano" title="Arenal Volcano">Arenal Volcano</a>, in Costa Rica, erupted and killed 87 people. Fertile soils from weathered volcanic lavas have made it possible to sustain dense populations in agriculturally productive highland areas.
</p><p>Central America has many <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain ranges</a>; the longest are the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Chiapas" title="Sierra Madre de Chiapas">Sierra Madre de Chiapas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Isabelia" title="Cordillera Isabelia">Cordillera Isabelia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_de_Talamanca" title="Cordillera de Talamanca">Cordillera de Talamanca</a>. Between the mountain ranges lie fertile valleys that are suitable for the people; in fact, most of the population of Honduras, Costa Rica, and Guatemala live in valleys. Valleys are also suitable for the production of coffee, beans, and other crops.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_North_America_present.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1816" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Koppen-Geiger_Map_North_America_present.svg/310px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_North_America_present.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Koppen-Geiger_Map_North_America_present.svg/465px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_North_America_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Koppen-Geiger_Map_North_America_present.svg/620px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_North_America_present.svg.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_North_America_present.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>North America map of Köppen climate classification</div></div></div>
<p>North America is a very large continent that extends from north of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">Arctic Circle</a> to south of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>. Greenland, along with the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">Canadian Shield</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> with average temperatures ranging from 10 to 20 °C (50 to 68 °F), but central Greenland is composed of a very large ice sheet. This tundra radiates throughout Canada, but its border ends near the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> (but still contains Alaska) and at the end of the Canadian Shield, near the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>.
Climate west of the <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Range" title="Cascade Range">Cascade Range</a> is described as being temperate weather with average precipitation 20 inches (510 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[72]</a></sup>
Climate in coastal California is described to be <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a>, with average temperatures in cities like <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> ranging from 57 to 70 °F (14 to 21 °C) over the course of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>Stretching from the East Coast to eastern North Dakota, and stretching down to Kansas, is the <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> featuring intense seasons, with a large amount of annual precipitation, with places like <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> averaging 50 inches (1,300 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[74]</a></sup>
Starting at the southern border of the humid continental climate and stretching to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> (whilst encompassing the eastern half of Texas) is the <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a>. This area has the wettest cities in the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a>, with annual precipitation reaching 67 inches (1,700 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile, Alabama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[75]</a></sup>
Stretching from the borders of the humid continental and subtropical climates, and going west to the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada" title="Sierra Nevada">Sierra Nevada</a>, south to the southern tip of <a href="/wiki/Durango" title="Durango">Durango</a>, north to the border with tundra climate, the <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">steppe</a>/<a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desert</a> climates are the driest in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[76]</a></sup> Highland climates cut from north to south of the continent, where <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropical</a> or <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climates</a> occur just below the tropics, as in central <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">Tropical climates</a> appear in the <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">island</a> regions and in the subcontinent's bottleneck. Precipitation patterns vary across the region, and as such <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">rainforest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">monsoon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">savanna</a> types can be found, with rains and high temperatures throughout the year. Found in countries and states bathed by the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> or to the south of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[77]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output
