<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_endangered_plants_in_North_America" title="List of endangered plants in North America">List of endangered plants in North America</a></div>
<p>Notable North American fauna include the <a href="/wiki/American_bison" title="American bison">bison</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_black_bear" title="American black bear">black bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">jaguar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">cougar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prairie_dog" title="Prairie dog">prairie dog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pronghorn" title="Pronghorn">pronghorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raccoon" title="Raccoon">raccoon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coyote" title="Coyote">coyote</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monarch_butterfly" title="Monarch butterfly">monarch butterfly</a>.
</p><p>Notable plants that were domesticated in North America include <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cucurbita" title="Cucurbita">squash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomato</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunflower" title="Sunflower">sunflower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blueberry" title="Blueberry">blueberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocado</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_cotton" title="Mexican cotton">cotton</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chile_pepper" title="Chile pepper">chile pepper</a>
and <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_America" title="History of North America">History of North America</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian">Pre-Columbian</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:America_1000_BCE.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2138" data-file-width="1407" decoding="async" height="334" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/America_1000_BCE.png/220px-America_1000_BCE.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/America_1000_BCE.png/330px-America_1000_BCE.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/America_1000_BCE.png/440px-America_1000_BCE.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:America_1000_BCE.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Simplified map of subsistence methods in the Americas at 1000 BCE <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FEFE00; color:black;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherers" title="Hunter-gatherers">hunter-gatherers</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#00FE00; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">simple farming societies</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FE7F3F; color:black;"> </span> complex farming societies (tribal <a href="/wiki/Chiefdom" title="Chiefdom">chiefdoms</a> or <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilizations</a>)</div></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples of the Americas</a> have many <a href="/wiki/Creation_myth" title="Creation myth">creation myths</a> by which they assert that they have been present on the land since its creation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtin2014_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Curtin2014-86">[78]</a></sup> but there is no evidence that humans evolved there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krensky_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Krensky-87">[79]</a></sup> The specifics of the initial <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_the_Americas" title="Settlement of the Americas">settlement of the Americas</a> by ancient Asians are subject to ongoing research and discussion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White2006_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-White2006-88">[80]</a></sup> The traditional theory has been that hunters entered the <a href="/wiki/Beringia" title="Beringia">Bering Land Bridge</a> between eastern <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> and present-day <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> from 27,000 to 14,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HavilandPrins2013_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-HavilandPrins2013-89">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sonneborn-2007_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sonneborn-2007-90">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[i]</a></sup> A growing viewpoint is that the first American inhabitants sailed from Beringia some 13,000 years ago,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[84]</a></sup> with widespread habitation of the Americas during the end of the <a href="/wiki/Last_Glacial_Period" title="Last Glacial Period">Last Glacial Period</a>, in what is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Glacial_Maximum#North_America" title="Late Glacial Maximum">Late Glacial Maximum</a>, around 12,500 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pauketat2012_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pauketat2012-94">[85]</a></sup> The oldest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petroglyphs" title="Petroglyphs">petroglyphs</a> in North America date from 15,000 to 10,000 years before present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[j]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetic_history_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Genetic history of indigenous peoples of the Americas">Genetic research</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a> indicate additional waves of migration from Asia via the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a> during the Early-Middle <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SkoglundMallick2015_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-SkoglundMallick2015-98">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BellwoodNess2014_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-BellwoodNess2014-99">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before contact with Europeans, the <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">natives of North America</a> were divided into many different polities, from small <a href="/wiki/Band_society" title="Band society">bands</a> of a few families to large empires. They lived in several "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classification_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Classification of indigenous peoples of the Americas">culture areas</a>", which roughly correspond to <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_North_America" title="Geography of North America">geographic and biological zones</a> and give a good indication of the main way of life of the people who lived there (e.g., the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plains_Bison" title="Plains Bison">bison</a> <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunters</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plains_Indian" title="Plains Indian">Great Plains</a>, or the farmers of <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>). Native groups can also be classified by their <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">language family</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Athabaskan_languages" title="Athabaskan languages">Athapascan</a> or <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Uto-Aztecan_languages" title="Uto-Aztecan languages">Uto-Aztecan</a></span>). Peoples with similar languages did not always share the same <a href="/wiki/Material_culture" title="Material culture">material culture</a>, nor were they always allies. Anthropologists think that the <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> of the high <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> came to North America much later than other native groups, as evidenced by the disappearance of <a href="/wiki/Dorset_culture" title="Dorset culture">Dorset culture</a> artifacts from the <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_record" title="Archaeological record">archaeological record</a>, and their replacement by the <a href="/wiki/Thule_people" title="Thule people">Thule people</a>.
</p><p>During the thousands of years of native habitation on the continent, cultures changed and shifted. One of the oldest yet discovered is the <a href="/wiki/Clovis_culture" title="Clovis culture">Clovis culture</a> (c. 9550–9050 BCE) in modern <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bradshaw_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-bradshaw-96">[87]</a></sup> Later groups include the <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">Mississippian culture</a> and related <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mound_builder_(people)" title="Mound builder (people)">Mound building</a> cultures, found in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippi_river" title="Mississippi river">Mississippi river</a> valley and the <a href="/wiki/Ancestral_Puebloans" title="Ancestral Puebloans">Pueblo culture</a> of what is now the <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners" title="Four Corners">Four Corners</a>. The more southern cultural groups of North America were responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domestication</a> of many common <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crops" title="Crops">crops</a> now used around the world, such as tomatoes, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squash_(plant)" title="Squash (plant)">squash</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>. As a result of the development of agriculture in the south, many other cultural advances were made there. The <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Mayans</a> developed a <a href="/wiki/Maya_script" title="Maya script">writing system</a>, built <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_pyramids" title="Mesoamerican pyramids">huge pyramids and temples</a>, had a <a href="/wiki/Maya_calendar" title="Maya calendar">complex calendar</a>, and developed the concept of zero around 400 CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first recorded European references to North America are in <a href="/wiki/Vinland_sagas" title="Vinland sagas">Norse sagas</a> where it is referred to as <a href="/wiki/Vinland" title="Vinland">Vinland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[92]</a></sup> The earliest verifiable instance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_trans-oceanic_contact" title="Pre-Columbian trans-oceanic contact">pre-Columbian trans-oceanic contact</a> by any European culture with the North America mainland has been dated to around 1000 CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows#Norse_site_(c._1000)" title="L'Anse aux Meadows">The site</a>, situated at the northernmost extent of the island named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a>, has provided unmistakable evidence of <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a> settlement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[94]</a></sup> Norse explorer <a href="/wiki/Leif_Erikson" title="Leif Erikson">Leif Erikson</a> (c. 970–1020 CE) is thought to have visited the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[k]</a></sup> Erikson was the first European to make landfall on the continent (excluding Greenland).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Mayan culture was still present in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yucatan_Peninsula" title="Yucatan Peninsula">southern Mexico</a> and Guatemala when the Spanish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquistadors" title="Conquistadors">conquistadors</a> arrived, but political dominance in the area had shifted to the <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">Aztec Empire</a>, whose capital city <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Tenochtitlan</a> was located further north in the <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Mexico" title="Valley of Mexico">Valley of Mexico</a>. The Aztecs were conquered in 1521 by <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grunberg_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grunberg-109">[98]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Post-contact.2C_1492.E2.80.931910"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-contact,_1492–1910">Post-contact, 1492–1910</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_European_colonization_of_North_America" title="Timeline of the European colonization of North America">Timeline of the European colonization of North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_America" title="French America">French America</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Russian colonization of the Americas">Russian colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:QueenAnnesWarBefore.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1090" data-file-width="1530" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/QueenAnnesWarBefore.svg/260px-QueenAnnesWarBefore.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/QueenAnnesWarBefore.svg/390px-QueenAnnesWarBefore.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/QueenAnnesWarBefore.svg/520px-QueenAnnesWarBefore.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:QueenAnnesWarBefore.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of North America in 1702 showing forts, towns and (in solid colors) areas occupied by European settlements</div></div></div>
<p>During the so-called <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, Europeans explored overseas and staked claims to various parts of North America, much of which was already settled by indigenous peoples. Upon Europeans' arrival in the "<a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>", indigenous peoples had a variety of reactions, including curiosity, trading, cooperation, resignation, and resistance. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Population_history_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Population history of indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous population declined</a> substantially following European arrival, primarily due to the introduction of Eurasian diseases, such as <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>, to which the indigenous peoples lacked immunity, and because of <a href="/wiki/American_Indian_Wars" title="American Indian Wars">violent conflicts</a> with Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[99]</a></sup> Indigenous culture changed significantly and their affiliation with political and cultural groups also changed. Several linguistic groups <a href="/wiki/Language_death" title="Language death">died out</a>, and others changed quite quickly.
</p><p>On the southern eastcoast of North America, Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de León">Juan Ponce de León</a>, who had accompanied Columbus's second voyage, visited and named in 1513 <i><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">La Florida</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[100]</a></sup> As the colonial period unfolded, Spain, England, and France appropriated and claimed extensive territories in North America eastern and southern coastlines. Spain established permanent settlements on the Caribbean islands of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> in the 1490s, building cities, putting the resident indigenous populations to work, raising crops for Spanish settlers and panning gold to enrich the Spaniards. Much of the indigenous population died due to disease and overwork, spurring the Spaniards on the claim new lands and peoples. An expedition under the command of Spanish settler, <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a>, sailed westward in 1519 to what turned out to be the mainland in Mexico. With local indigenous allies, the Spanish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec empire">conquered the Aztec empire in central Mexico</a> in 1521. Spain then established permanent cities in Mexico, Central America, and Spanish South America in the sixteenth century. Once Spaniards conquered the high civilization of the Aztecs and Incas, the Caribbean was a backwater of the Spanish empire.
</p><p>Other European powers began to intrude on areas that Spain had claimed, including the Caribbean islands. France took the western half of Hispaniola and developed <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a> as a cane sugar producing colony worked by black slave labor. Britain took <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>; the Dutch and Danes also took islands previous claimed by Spain. Britain did not begin settling on the North American mainland until a hundred years after the first Spanish settlements, since it sought first to control nearby Ireland. The first permanent English settlement was in <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown, Virginia</a> in 1607, and then further settler colonial establishments on the east coast of the continent from is now Georgia up to Massachusetts, forming the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>. The English did not establish settlements north, east of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River_Valley" title="St. Lawrence River Valley">St. Lawrence Valley</a> in what would become Canada until well after the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">war of independence</a>. English early permanent settlements were <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="St. John's, Newfoundland and Labrador">St. John's, Newfoundland</a> in 1630 and <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax, Nova Scotia</a> in 1749. The first permanent French settlement was in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quebec_City,_Quebec" title="Quebec City, Quebec">Quebec City, Quebec</a> in 1608. In the British victory the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, France ceded to Britain its claims east of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> in 1763. Spain gained rights to the territories west of Mississippi now acting as a border. French so-called "colonists" that had first settled the <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Country" title="Illinois Country">Illinois Country</a> after several generations of experience on the new continent migrated over the Mississippi in the absence of Spanish occupants while leveraging earlier Louisiana French settlements around the Gulf of Mexico. These early French settlers partnering with midwest indigenous tribes and their mixed ancestry descendants would precede the westward push and guide through waves of followers all the way to the Pacific.
</p><p>In the late 18th and early the Thirteen Colonies on the North Atlantic coast declared independence in 1776, fighting a protracted <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">war of independence</a> with the aid of Britain's enemies France and Spain, becoming the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_of_America" title="United States of America">United States of America</a>. The new nation steadily attempted to increase its territory. By that time, Russians were already well established on the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a> northern coastline with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maritime_Fur_Trade" title="Maritime Fur Trade">Maritime Fur Trade</a> activities supported by active settlements. As a result, Spanish were showing more interest in controlling the trade on the Pacific coast and mapped most of its coastline. The first Spanish settlements were attempted in <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> during that period. Numerous overland explorations associated with <a href="/wiki/Voyageurs" title="Voyageurs">Voyageurs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fur_Trade" title="Fur Trade">Fur Trade</a>, and United States led expeditions (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Clark_Expedition" title="Lewis and Clark Expedition">Lewis and Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_C._Fr%C3%A9mont" title="John C. Frémont">Fremont</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Exploring_Expedition" title="United States Exploring Expedition">Wilkes</a>) were reaching the Pacific at various latitudes around the turn of the century. In 1803 Napoleon Bonaparte sold France's remaining claims in North America, west of the Mississippi River, to the United States, in a deal named the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a>. Spain and the United States settled their western boundary dispute in 1819 in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adams-On%C3%ADs_Treaty" title="Adams-Onís Treaty">Adams-Onís Treaty</a>. Mexico fought a lengthy war for independence from Spain, winning it for Mexico and Central American in 1821. The U.S. sought further westward expansion and fought the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican-American_War" title="Mexican-American War">Mexican-American War</a>, gaining a vast territory that first Spain and then Mexico claimed but which they did not effectively control. Much of the area was in fact dominated by indigenous peoples, which did not recognize the claims of Spain, France, or the United States. Russia sold its North American claims, which included Alaska, to the U.S. in 1867. Also in 1867, settler colonies in eastern North America, were unified as the dominion of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The U.S. sought to dig a canal across the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a>, a part of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, and aided Panamanians in a war to separate it from Colombia. The U.S. carved out the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal_Zone" title="Panama Canal Zone">Panama Canal Zone</a>, over which it claimed sovereignty. After decades of work on the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a> was completed, connecting the Atlantic and Pacific oceans in 1913.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_United_States" title="Demographics of the United States">Demographics of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Canada" title="Demographics of Canada">Demographics of Canada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Mexico" title="Demographics of Mexico">Demographics of Mexico</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="783" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif/220px-Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif/330px-Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif/440px-Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Non-native nations' control and claims over North America c. 1750–2008</div></div></div>
<p>Economically, Canada and the United States are the wealthiest and most <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed nations</a> in the continent, followed by Mexico, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newly_industrialized_countries" title="Newly industrialized countries">newly industrialized country</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIA_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-AIA-112">[101]</a></sup> The countries of Central America and the Caribbean are at various levels of economic and human development. For example, small Caribbean island-nations, such as Barbados, Trinidad and Tobago, and Antigua and Barbuda, have a higher <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP (PPP) per capita</a> than Mexico due to their smaller populations. Panama and Costa Rica have a significantly higher <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> and GDP than the rest of the Central American nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-113">[102]</a></sup> Additionally, despite Greenland's vast resources in oil and minerals, much of them remain untapped, and the island is economically dependent on fishing, tourism, and subsidies from Denmark. Nevertheless, the island is highly developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Demographically, North America is ethnically diverse. Its three main groups are <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">Whites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Blacks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Composed_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Composed-115">[104]</a></sup> There is a significant minority of Indigenous Americans and <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asians</a> among other less numerous groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Composed_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-Composed-115">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_North_America" title="Languages of North America">Languages of North America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Langs_N.Amer.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1170" data-file-width="1290" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Langs_N.Amer.png/220px-Langs_N.Amer.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Langs_N.Amer.png/330px-Langs_N.Amer.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Langs_N.Amer.png/440px-Langs_N.Amer.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Langs_N.Amer.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">Native languages</a> of the US, Canada, Greenland, and Northern Mexico</div></div></div>
<p>The dominant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages_in_North_America" title="Languages in North America">languages in North America</a> are English, Spanish, and French. Danish is prevalent in Greenland alongside <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic</a>, and Dutch is spoken side by side local languages in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Dutch Caribbean</a>. The term Anglo-America is used to refer to the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">anglophone</a> countries of the Americas: namely Canada (where English and French are co-official) and the United States, but also sometimes Belize and parts of the tropics, especially the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Caribbean" title="Commonwealth Caribbean">Commonwealth Caribbean</a>. Latin America refers to the other areas of the Americas (generally south of the United States) where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">Romance languages</a>, derived from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>, of Spanish and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, (but French-speaking countries are not usually included) predominate: the other republics of Central America (but not always Belize), part of the Caribbean (not the Dutch-, English-, or French-speaking areas), Mexico, and most of South America (except <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> (France), and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> (UK)).
</p><p>The French language has historically played a significant role in North America and now retains a distinctive presence in some regions. Canada is officially bilingual. French is the official language of the Province of Quebec, where 95% of the people speak it as either their first or second language, and it is co-official with English in the Province of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>. Other French-speaking locales include the Province of <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> (the official language is English, but there are an estimated 600,000 Franco-Ontarians), the Province of <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a> (co-official as <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> with English), the <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre_et_Miquelon" title="Saint-Pierre et Miquelon">Saint-Pierre et Miquelon</a>, as well as the US state of Louisiana, where French is also an official language. Haiti is included with this group based on historical association but Haitians speak both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole_language" title="Haitian Creole language">Creole</a> and French. Similarly, French and French Antillean Creole is spoken in Saint Lucia and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Dominica" title="Commonwealth of Dominica">Commonwealth of Dominica</a> alongside English.
</p><p>A significant number of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Indigenous languages</a> are spoken in North America, with 372,000 people in the United States speaking an indigenous language at home,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[105]</a></sup> about 225,000 in Canada<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[106]</a></sup> and roughly 6 million in Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[107]</a></sup> In the United States and Canada, there are approximately 150 surviving indigenous languages of the 300 spoken prior to European contact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_North_America" title="Religion in North America">Religion in North America</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religions_of_the_world" title="Religions of the world">Religions of the world</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_America_Religious_Belief.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="934" data-file-width="721" decoding="async" height="337" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/North_America_Religious_Belief.svg/260px-North_America_Religious_Belief.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/North_America_Religious_Belief.svg/390px-North_America_Religious_Belief.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/North_America_Religious_Belief.svg/520px-North_America_Religious_Belief.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:North_America_Religious_Belief.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Percentage of people who identify with a religion in North America, according to 2010–2012 data</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the largest religion in the United States, Canada and Mexico. According to a 2012 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> survey, 77% of the population considered themselves <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[109]</a></sup> Christianity also is the predominant religion <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_North_America" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in North America">in the 23 dependent territories in North America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[110]</a></sup> The United States has the <a href="/wiki/Christianity_by_country" title="Christianity by country">largest Christian population</a> in the world, with nearly 247 million Christians (70%), although other countries have higher percentages of Christians among their populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[111]</a></sup> Mexico has the world's second largest number of Catholics, surpassed only by <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[112]</a></sup> A 2015 study estimates about 493,000 Christian believers from a Muslim background in North America, most of them belonging to some form of Protestantism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the same study, the <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">religiously unaffiliated</a> (including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agnostic" title="Agnostic">agnostics</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atheist" title="Atheist">atheists</a>) make up about 17% of the population of Canada and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Religiously_Unaffiliated_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Religiously_Unaffiliated-125">[114]</a></sup> Those with no religious affiliation make up about 24% of the United States population, and 24% of Canada's total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion2011_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-religion2011-126">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>Canada, the United States and Mexico host communities of <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> (6 million or about 1.8%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[116]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhists" title="Buddhists">Buddhists</a> (3.8 million or 1.1%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[117]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> (3.4 million or 1.0%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[118]</a></sup> The largest number of Jews can be found in the United States (5.4 million),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[119]</a></sup> Canada (375,000)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[120]</a></sup> and Mexico (67,476).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INEGI_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-INEGI-132">[121]</a></sup> The United States hosts the largest Muslim population in North America with 2.7 million or 0.9%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew2015_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-pew2015-133">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Islam_in_the_United_States_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Islam_in_the_United_States-134">[123]</a></sup> While Canada host about one million Muslim or 3.2% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[124]</a></sup> While in Mexico there were 3,700 Muslims in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010-census_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-136">[125]</a></sup> In 2012, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U-T_San_Diego" title="U-T San Diego">U-T San Diego</a></i> estimated U.S. practitioners of Buddhism at 1.2 million people, of whom 40% are living in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>The predominant religion in Mexico and Central America is Christianity (96%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christianity_in_its_Global_Context_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Christianity_in_its_Global_Context-138">[127]</a></sup> Beginning with the Spanish colonization of Mexico in the 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a> was the only religion permitted by Spanish crown and Catholic church. A vast campaign of religious conversion, the so-called "spiritual conquest", was launched to bring indigenous into the Christian fold. The <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Inquisition" title="Mexican Inquisition">Inquisition</a> was established to assure orthodox belief and practice. The Catholic Church remained an important institution, so that even after political independence, Roman Catholicism remained the dominant religion. Since the 1960s, there has been an increase in other Christian groups, particularly <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, as well as other religious organizations, and individuals identifying themselves as having no religion. Also Christianity is the predominant religion in the Caribbean (85%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christianity_in_its_Global_Context_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-Christianity_in_its_Global_Context-138">[127]</a></sup> Other religious groups in the region are <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rastafari" title="Rastafari">Rastafari</a> (in Jamaica), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-American_religions" title="Afro-American religions">Afro-American religions</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa" title="Santería">Santería</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Vodou" title="Haitian Vodou">Vodou</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Populace">Populace</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_North_American_countries_by_population" title="List of North American countries by population">List of North American countries by population</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_North_American_cities_by_population" title="List of North American cities by population">List of North American cities by population</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_North_American_metropolitan_areas_by_population" title="List of North American metropolitan areas by population">List of North American metropolitan areas by population</a></div>

class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a href="/wiki/Guadalajara_metropolitan_area" title="Guadalajara metropolitan area">Guadalajara</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>North America is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_continents_by_population" title="List of continents by population">fourth</a> most populous continent after Asia, Africa, and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[128]</a></sup> Its most populous country is the United States with 329.7 million persons. The second largest country is Mexico with a population of 112.3 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INEGI_2010_Census_Statistics_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-INEGI_2010_Census_Statistics-140">[129]</a></sup> Canada is the third most populous country with 37.0 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[130]</a></sup> The majority of Caribbean island-nations have national populations under a million, though Cuba, Dominican Republic, Haiti, Puerto Rico (a territory of the United States), Jamaica, and Trinidad and Tobago each have populations higher than a million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cubastat_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-cubastat-142">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prez_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-prez-143">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[135]</a></sup> Greenland has a small population of 55,984 for its massive size (2,166,000 km<sup>2</sup> or 836,300 mi<sup>2</sup>), and therefore, it has the world's lowest population density at 0.026 pop./km<sup>2</sup> (0.067 pop./mi<sup>2</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>While the United States, Canada, and Mexico maintain the largest populations, large city populations are not restricted to those nations. There are also large cities in the Caribbean. The largest cities in North America, by far, are Mexico City and New York. These cities are the only cities on the continent to exceed eight million, and two of three in the Americas. Next in size are Los Angeles, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[137]</a></sup> Chicago, Havana, Santo Domingo, and <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>. Cities in the <a href="/wiki/Sun_Belt" title="Sun Belt">sun belt</a> regions of the United States, such as those in Southern California and <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix</a>, Miami, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas</a>, are experiencing rapid growth. These causes included warm temperatures, retirement of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baby_Boomers" title="Baby Boomers">Baby Boomers</a>, large industry, and the influx of immigrants. Cities near the United States border, particularly in Mexico, are also experiencing large amounts of growth. Most notable is <a href="/wiki/Tijuana" title="Tijuana">Tijuana</a>, a city bordering San Diego that receives immigrants from all over Latin America and parts of Europe and Asia. Yet as cities grow in these warmer regions of North America, they are increasingly forced to deal with the major issue of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_shortages" title="Water shortages">water shortages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>Eight of the top ten <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_areas" title="Metropolitan areas">metropolitan areas</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="Table of United States Metropolitan Statistical Areas">are located in the United States</a>. These metropolitan areas all have a population of above 5.5 million and include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City_metropolitan_area" title="New York City metropolitan area">New York City metropolitan area</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area" title="Los Angeles metropolitan area">Los Angeles metropolitan area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_metropolitan_area" title="Chicago metropolitan area">Chicago metropolitan area</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCBSA_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-150">[139]</a></sup> Whilst the majority of the largest metropolitan areas are within the United States, Mexico is host to the largest metropolitan area by population in North America: <a href="/wiki/Greater_Mexico_City" title="Greater Mexico City">Greater Mexico City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[140]</a></sup> Canada also breaks into the top ten largest metropolitan areas with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toronto_metropolitan_area" title="Toronto metropolitan area">Toronto metropolitan area</a> having six million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statcan2006_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-statcan2006-152">[141]</a></sup> The proximity of cities to each other on the <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Canada–United States border">Canada–United States border</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Mexico–United States border">Mexico–United States border</a> has led to the rise of international metropolitan areas. These <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_agglomerations" title="Urban agglomerations">urban agglomerations</a> are observed at their largest and most productive in <a href="/wiki/Detroit%E2%80%93Windsor" title="Detroit–Windsor">Detroit–Windsor</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego%E2%80%93Tijuana" title="San Diego–Tijuana">San Diego–Tijuana</a> and experience large commercial, economic, and cultural activity. The metropolitan areas are responsible for millions of dollars of trade dependent on international freight. In Detroit-Windsor the Border Transportation Partnership study in 2004 concluded US$13 billion was dependent on the Detroit–Windsor international border crossing while in San Diego-Tijuana freight at the Otay Mesa Port of Entry was valued at US$20 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planning_SD-TJ_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Planning_SD-TJ-154">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Megaregions_of_the_United_States" title="Megaregions of the United States">Megaregions of the United States</a></div>
<p>North America has also been witness to the growth of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megapolitan_area" title="Megapolitan area">megapolitan areas</a>. In the United States exists eleven megaregions that transcend international borders and comprise Canadian and Mexican metropolitan regions. These are the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Sun_Corridor" title="Arizona Sun Corridor">Arizona Sun Corridor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Cascadia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Megalopolis" title="Great Lakes Megalopolis">Great Lakes Megalopolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">Gulf Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">Northeast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">Northern California</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piedmont_Atlantic" title="Piedmont Atlantic">Piedmont Atlantic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_California_Megaregion" title="Southern California Megaregion">Southern California</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Triangle" title="Texas Triangle">Texas Triangle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[144]</a></sup> Canada and Mexico are also the home of megaregions. These include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quebec_City_%E2%80%93_Windsor_Corridor" title="Quebec City – Windsor Corridor">Quebec City – Windsor Corridor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horseshoe" title="Golden Horseshoe">Golden Horseshoe</a> – both of which are considered part of the Great Lakes Megalopolis – and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Mexico_megalopolis" title="Central Mexico megalopolis">Central Mexico megalopolis</a>. Traditionally the largest megaregion has been considered the Boston-Washington, DC Corridor, or the Northeast, as the region is one massive contiguous area. Yet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_megapolitan_areas#Planning" title="United States megapolitan areas">megaregion criterion</a> have allowed the Great Lakes Megalopolis to maintain status as the most populated region, being home to 53,768,125 people in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPA08_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-RPA08-156">[145]</a></sup>
</p><p>The top ten largest North American <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan areas</a> by population as of 2013, based on national census numbers from the United States and census estimates from Canada and Mexico.
</p>

<td>9</td>

<tr>
<td>10</td>
<td align="left"><span class="nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="1005" decoding="async" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg/23px-Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg/35px-Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg/46px-Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a></span></td>
<td>30,720</td>
<td>2022
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>North America's GDP per capita was evaluated in October 2016 by the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) to be $41,830, making it the richest continent in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFcapitaGDP_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMFcapitaGDP-159">[148]</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-us_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-us-160">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>Canada, Mexico, and the United States have significant and multifaceted economic systems. The United States has the largest economy of all three countries and in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-us_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-us-160">[149]</a></sup> In 2016, the U.S. had an estimated per capita gross domestic product (PPP) of $57,466 according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, and is the most technologically developed economy of the three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[150]</a></sup> The United States' services sector comprises 77% of the country's GDP (estimated in 2010), industry comprises 22% and agriculture comprises 1.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-us_160-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-us-160">[149]</a></sup> The U.S. economy is also the fastest growing economy in North America and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> as a whole,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFcapitaGDP_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-IMFcapitaGDP-159">[148]</a></sup> with the highest GDP per capita in the Americas as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFcapitaGDP_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-IMFcapitaGDP-159">[148]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Donald_J._Trump_at_the_G20_Summit_(44300765490).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/President_Donald_J._Trump_at_the_G20_Summit_%2844300765490%29.jpg/220px-President_Donald_J._Trump_at_the_G20_Summit_%2844300765490%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/President_Donald_J._Trump_at_the_G20_Summit_%2844300765490%29.jpg/330px-President_Donald_J._Trump_at_the_G20_Summit_%2844300765490%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/President_Donald_J._Trump_at_the_G20_Summit_%2844300765490%29.jpg/440px-President_Donald_J._Trump_at_the_G20_Summit_%2844300765490%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Donald_J._Trump_at_the_G20_Summit_(44300765490).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mexican President <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto" title="Enrique Peña Nieto">Peña Nieto</a>, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Trump</a>, and Canadian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Trudeau</a> sign the <a href="/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Mexico%E2%80%93Canada_Agreement" title="United States–Mexico–Canada Agreement">United States–Mexico–Canada Agreement</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2018_G20_Buenos_Aires_summit" title="2018 G20 Buenos Aires summit">G20 summit</a> in Buenos Aires, Argentina, on 30 November 2018</div></div></div>
<p>Canada shows significant growth in the sectors of services, mining and manufacturing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-ca_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-ca-163">[152]</a></sup> Canada's per capita GDP (PPP) was estimated at $44,656 and it had the 11th largest GDP (nominal) in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-ca_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-ca-163">[152]</a></sup> Canada's services sector comprises 78% of the country's GDP (estimated in 2010), industry comprises 20% and agriculture comprises 2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-ca_163-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-ca-163">[152]</a></sup> Mexico has a per capita GDP (PPP) of $16,111 and as of 2014 is the 15th largest GDP (nominal) in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imf-mx_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-imf-mx-164">[153]</a></sup> Being a <a href="/wiki/Newly_industrialized_country" title="Newly industrialized country">newly industrialized country</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIA_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-AIA-112">[101]</a></sup> Mexico maintains both modern and outdated industrial and agricultural facilities and operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-mex_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-mex-165">[154]</a></sup> Its main sources of income are oil, industrial exports, manufactured goods, electronics, heavy industry, automobiles, construction, food, banking and financial services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>The North American economy is well defined and structured in three main economic areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UANL_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-UANL-167">[156]</a></sup> These areas are the North American Free Trade Agreement (NAFTA), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community_and_Common_Market" title="Caribbean Community and Common Market">Caribbean Community and Common Market</a> (CARICOM), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Common_Market" title="Central American Common Market">Central American Common Market</a> (CACM).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UANL_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-UANL-167">[156]</a></sup> Of these trade blocs, the United States takes part in two. In addition to the larger trade blocs there is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada-Costa_Rica_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Canada-Costa Rica Free Trade Agreement">Canada-Costa Rica Free Trade Agreement</a> among numerous other free trade relations, often between the larger, more developed countries and Central American and Caribbean countries.
</p><p>The North America Free Trade Agreement (NAFTA) forms one of the four largest trade blocs in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[157]</a></sup> Its implementation in 1994 was designed for economic homogenization with hopes of eliminating barriers of trade and foreign investment between Canada, the United States and Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[158]</a></sup> While Canada and the United States already conducted the largest bilateral trade relationship – and to present day still do – in the world and <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_trade_relations" title="Canada–United States trade relations">Canada–United States trade relations</a> already allowed trade without national taxes and tariffs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[159]</a></sup> NAFTA allowed Mexico to experience a similar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duty-free" title="Duty-free">duty-free</a> trade. The free trade agreement allowed for the elimination of tariffs that had previously been in place on United States-Mexico trade. Trade volume has steadily increased annually and in 2010, surface trade between the three NAFTA nations reached an all-time historical increase of 24.3% or US$791 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[160]</a></sup> The NAFTA trade bloc GDP (PPP) is the world's largest with US$17.617 trillion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[161]</a></sup> This is in part attributed to the fact that the economy of the United States is the world's largest national economy; the country had a nominal GDP of approximately $14.7 trillion in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bea2011_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-bea2011-173">[162]</a></sup> The countries of NAFTA are also some of each other's largest trade partners. The United States is the largest trade partner of Canada and Mexico;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[163]</a></sup> while Canada and Mexico are each other's third largest trade partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth(in_trillions_USD),_2018.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1334" data-file-width="1889" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg/220px-Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg/330px-Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg/440px-Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth(in_trillions_USD),_2018.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Worlds regions by total wealth (in trillions USD), 2018</div></div></div>
<p>The Caribbean trade bloc – CARICOM – came into agreement in 1973 when it was signed by 15 Caribbean nations. As of 2000, CARICOM trade volume was US$96 billion. CARICOM also allowed for the creation of a <a href="/wiki/CARICOM_passport" title="CARICOM passport">common passport</a> for associated nations. In the past decade the trade bloc focused largely on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Free Trade Agreement">Free Trade Agreements</a> and under the CARICOM Office of Trade Negotiations (OTN) free trade agreements have been signed into effect.
</p><p>Integration of Central American economies occurred under the signing of the Central American Common Market agreement in 1961; this was the first attempt to engage the nations of this area into stronger financial cooperation. The recent implementation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central American Free Trade Agreement">Central American Free Trade Agreement</a> (CAFTA) has left the future of the CACM unclear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[166]</a></sup> The Central American Free Trade Agreement was signed by five Central American countries, the Dominican Republic, and the United States. The focal point of CAFTA is to create a free trade area similar to that of NAFTA. In addition to the United States, Canada also has relations in Central American trade blocs. Currently under proposal, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada_%E2%80%93_Central_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Canada – Central American Free Trade Agreement">Canada – Central American Free Trade Agreement</a> (CA4) would operate much the same as CAFTA with the United States does.
</p><p>These nations also take part in inter-continental trade blocs. Mexico takes a part in the <a href="/wiki/G3_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="G3 Free Trade Agreement">G3 Free Trade Agreement</a> with Colombia and Venezuela and has a trade agreement with the EU. The United States has proposed and maintained trade agreements under the <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_Free_Trade_Area" title="Transatlantic Free Trade Area">Transatlantic Free Trade Area</a> between itself and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US-Middle_East_Free_Trade_Area" title="US-Middle East Free Trade Area">US-Middle East Free Trade Area</a> between numerous Middle Eastern nations and itself; and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Strategic_Economic_Partnership" title="Trans-Pacific Strategic Economic Partnership">Trans-Pacific Strategic Economic Partnership</a> between Southeast Asian nations, Australia, and New Zealand.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport"><span id="Infrastructure">Transport</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_North_America" title="Transportation in North America">Transportation in North America</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pan-American_Highway" title="Pan-American Highway">Pan-American Highway</a> route in the Americas is the portion of a network of roads nearly 48,000 km (30,000 mi) in length which travels through the mainland nations. No definitive length of the Pan-American Highway exists because the US and Canadian governments have never officially defined any specific routes as being part of the Pan-American Highway, and Mexico officially has many branches connecting to the US border. However, the total length of the portion from Mexico to the northern extremity of the highway is roughly 26,000 km (16,000 mi).
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Class1rr.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Class1rr.png/220px-Class1rr.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Class1rr.png/330px-Class1rr.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Class1rr.png/440px-Class1rr.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Class1rr.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2006 map of the North American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_I_railroad" title="Class I railroad">Class I railroad</a> network</div></div></div>
<p>The First Transcontinental Railroad in the United States was built in the 1860s, linking the railroad network of the eastern US with California on the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> coast. Finished on 10 May 1869 at the famous <a href="/wiki/Golden_spike" title="Golden spike">golden spike</a> event at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Promontory_Summit,_Utah" title="Promontory Summit, Utah">Promontory Summit, Utah</a>, it created a nationwide mechanized transportation network that revolutionized the population and economy of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._West" title="U.S. West">American West</a>, catalyzing the transition from the <a href="/wiki/Wagon_train" title="Wagon train">wagon trains</a> of previous decades to a modern transportation system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-178">[167]</a></sup> Although an accomplishment, it achieved the status of first transcontinental railroad by connecting myriad eastern US railroads to the Pacific and was not the largest single railroad system in the world. The Canadian <a href="/wiki/Grand_Trunk_Railway" title="Grand Trunk Railway">Grand Trunk Railway</a> (GTR) had, by 1867, already accumulated more than 2,055 km (1,277 mi) of track by connecting Ontario with the Canadian Atlantic provinces west as far as <a href="/wiki/Port_Huron,_Michigan" title="Port Huron, Michigan">Port Huron, Michigan</a>, through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarnia,_Ontario" title="Sarnia, Ontario">Sarnia, Ontario</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span></h3>
<p>A shared telephone system known as the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan" title="North American Numbering Plan">North American Numbering Plan</a> (NANP) is an integrated <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">telephone numbering plan</a> of 24 countries and territories: the United States and its <a href="/wiki/Insular_area" title="Insular area">territories</a>, Canada, Bermuda, and 17 <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> nations.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1616" data-file-width="2154" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg/220px-Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg/330px-Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg/440px-Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">Baseball</a> is traditionally known as America's national pastime, but is also played in Canada, and many Latin American countries as well.</div></div></div>
<p>The cultures of North America are diverse. The United States and English Canada have many cultural similarities, while French Canada has a distinct culture from Anglophone Canada, which is protected by law. Since United States was formed from portions previously part of the Spanish Empire and then independent Mexico, and there has been considerable and continuing immigration of Spanish speakers from south of the U.S.-Mexico border. In the southwest of the U.S. there are many Hispanic cultural traditions and considerable bilingualism. Mexico and Central America are part of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and are culturally distinct from anglophone and francophone North America. However, they share with the United States the establishment of post-independence governments that are federated representative republics with written constitutions dating from their founding as nations. Canada is a federated parliamentary democracy under a constitutional monarchy.
</p><p>Canada's <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Canada" title="Constitution of Canada">constitution</a> dates to 1867, with confederation, in the British North America Act, but not until 1982 did Canada have the power to amend its own constitution. Canada's Francophone heritage has been enshrined in law since the British parliament passed the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Act" title="Quebec Act">Quebec Act</a> of 1774. In contrast to largely Protestant Anglo settlers in North America, French-speaking Canadians were Catholic and with the Quebec Act were guaranteed freedom to practice their religion, restored the right of the Catholic Church to impose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tithes" title="Tithes">tithes</a> for its support, and established French civil law in most circumstances.
</p><p>The distinctiveness of French language and culture has been codified in Canadian law, so that both English and French are designated official languages.  The U.S. has no official language, but its national language is English.
</p><p>The Canadian government took action to protect <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_culture" title="Canadian culture">Canadian culture</a> by limiting non-<a href="/wiki/Canadian_content" title="Canadian content">Canadian content</a> in broadcasting, creating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Radio_and_Telecommunications_Commission" title="Canadian Radio and Telecommunications Commission">Canadian Radio and Telecommunications Commission</a> (CRTC) to monitor Canadian content. In Quebec, the provincial government established the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Office_Quebecois_de_la_Langue_Francaise" title="Office Quebecois de la Langue Francaise">Quebec Office of the French Language</a>, often called the "language police" by Anglophones, which mandates the use of French terminology and signage in French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[168]</a></sup> Since 1968 the unicameral legislature has been called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quebec_National_Assembly" title="Quebec National Assembly">Quebec National Assembly</a>. <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-Baptiste_Day" title="Saint-Jean-Baptiste Day">Saint-Jean-Baptiste Day</a>, June 24, is the national holiday of Quebec and celebrated by francophone Canadians throughout Canada. In Quebec, the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Quebec" title="Education in Quebec">school system</a> was divided into Catholic and Protestant, so-called confessional schools. Anglophone education in Quebec has been increasingly undermined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_culture" title="Latino culture">Latino culture</a> is strong in the southwest of the U.S., as well as Florida, which draws Latin Americans from many countries in the hemisphere.  Northern Mexico, particularly in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">Monterrey</a>, Tijuana, <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Ciudad Juárez">Ciudad Juárez</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mexicali" title="Mexicali">Mexicali</a>, is strongly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States" title="Culture of the United States">culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_way" title="American way">way of life of the United States</a>.  Monterrey, a modern city with a significant industrial group, has been regarded as the most <a href="/wiki/Americanization" title="Americanization">Americanized</a> city in Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MonterreyFall_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-MonterreyFall-181">[170]</a></sup> Northern Mexico, the Western United States and <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, Canada share a <a href="/wiki/Cowboy" title="Cowboy">cowboy</a> culture.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglophone_Caribbean" title="Anglophone Caribbean">Anglophone Caribbean states</a> have witnessed and participated in the decline of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> and its influence on the region, and its replacement by the economic influence of Northern America in the Anglophone Caribbean. This is partly due to the relatively small populations of the English-speaking Caribbean countries, and also because many of them now have more people <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">living abroad</a> than those remaining at home.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Greenland has experienced many immigration waves from <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">Northern Canada</a>, e .g. the <a href="/wiki/Thule_people" title="Thule people">Thule People</a>. Therefore, Greenland shares some cultural ties with the indigenous peoples of Canada. Greenland is also considered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nordic_Countries" title="Nordic Countries">Nordic</a> and has strong Danish ties due to <a href="/wiki/Danish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Danish colonization of the Americas">centuries of colonization by Denmark</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[171]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Popular_culture_.E2.80.93_sports"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture_–_sports">Popular culture – sports</span></h3>
<p>The U.S. and Canada have major sports teams that compete against each other, including baseball, basketball, hockey, and soccer/football.
Canada, Mexico and the US submitted a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_America_2026_FIFA_World_Cup_bid" title="North America 2026 FIFA World Cup bid">joint bid to host</a> the <a href="/wiki/2026_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2026 FIFA World Cup">2026 FIFA World Cup</a>.
The following table shows the most prominent sports leagues in North America, in order of average revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[173]</a></sup> Canada has a separate <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">Canadian Football League</a> from the U.S. teams.
</p><p>The Native American game of <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse_in_Canada" title="Lacrosse in Canada">lacrosse</a> is considered a national sport in Canada. <a href="/wiki/Curling" title="Curling">Curling</a> is an important winter sport in Canada, and the Winter Olympics includes it in the roster. The English sport of <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_Canada" title="Cricket in Canada">cricket</a> is popular in parts of anglophone Canada and very popular in parts of the former British empire, but in Canada is considered a minor sport. Boxing is also a major sport in some countries, such as Mexico, Panama and Puerto Rico, and it's considered one of the main individual sports in the United States.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-one-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-one_51-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since the <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">Lucayan Archipelago</a> is located in the Atlantic Ocean rather than <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a> are part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> but are not technically part of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, although the United Nations groups them with the Caribbean.</span>
